     <h1 class="api-title">String</h1> 
     <p> <code class="api-signature"> public final class String </code> <br> <code class="api-signature"> extends <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/Object.html">Object</a> </code> <code class="api-signature"> implements <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/io/Serializable.html">Serializable</a>, <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/Comparable.html">Comparable</a>&lt;<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a>&gt;, <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/CharSequence.html">CharSequence</a> </code> </p>
     <table class="jd-inheritance-table"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td colspan="2" class="jd-inheritance-class-cell"><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/Object.html">java.lang.Object</a> </td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td class="jd-inheritance-space">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?</td> 
        <td colspan="1" class="jd-inheritance-class-cell">java.lang.String </td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <br>
     <hr> 
     <p>The <code>String</code> class represents character strings. All string literals in Java programs, such as <code>"abc"</code>, are implemented as instances of this class. </p>
     <p> Strings are constant; their values cannot be changed after they are created. String buffers support mutable strings. Because String objects are immutable they can be shared. For example: </p>
     <blockquote>
      <pre>
     String str = "abc";
 </pre>
     </blockquote>
     <p> is equivalent to: </p>
     <blockquote>
      <pre>
     char data[] = {'a', 'b', 'c'};
     String str = new String(data);
 </pre>
     </blockquote>
     <p> Here are some more examples of how strings can be used: </p>
     <blockquote>
      <pre>
     System.out.println("abc");
     String cde = "cde";
     System.out.println("abc" + cde);
     String c = "abc".substring(2,3);
     String d = cde.substring(1, 2);
 </pre>
     </blockquote> 
     <p> The class <code>String</code> includes methods for examining individual characters of the sequence, for comparing strings, for searching strings, for extracting substrings, and for creating a copy of a string with all characters translated to uppercase or to lowercase. Case mapping is based on the Unicode Standard version specified by the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/Character.html">Character</a></code> class. </p>
     <p> The Java language provides special support for the string concatenation operator (&nbsp;+&nbsp;), and for conversion of other objects to strings. String concatenation is implemented through the <code>StringBuilder</code>(or <code>StringBuffer</code>) class and its <code>append</code> method. String conversions are implemented through the method <code>toString</code>, defined by <code>Object</code> and inherited by all classes in Java. For additional information on string concatenation and conversion, see Gosling, Joy, and Steele, <i>The Java Language Specification</i>. </p>
     <p> Unless otherwise noted, passing a <tt>null</tt> argument to a constructor or method in this class will cause a <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/NullPointerException.html">NullPointerException</a></code> to be thrown. </p>
     <p>A <code>String</code> represents a string in the UTF-16 format in which <em>supplementary characters</em> are represented by <em>surrogate pairs</em> (see the section <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/Character.html#unicode">Unicode Character Representations</a> in the <code>Character</code> class for more information). Index values refer to <code>char</code> code units, so a supplementary character uses two positions in a <code>String</code>. </p>
     <p>The <code>String</code> class provides methods for dealing with Unicode code points (i.e., characters), in addition to those for dealing with Unicode code units (i.e., <code>char</code> values).</p> 
     <div> 
      <p><b>See also:</b></p> 
      <ul class="nolist">
       <li><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/Object.html#toString()">toString()</a></code></li>
       <li><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/StringBuffer.html">StringBuffer</a></code></li>
       <li><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/StringBuilder.html">StringBuilder</a></code></li>
       <li><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/nio/charset/Charset.html">Charset</a></code></li> 
      </ul> 
     </div>

     <!-- ========= FIELD DETAIL ======== --> 
     <h2 class="api-section">Fields</h2> 
     <a name="CASE_INSENSITIVE_ORDER"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">CASE_INSENSITIVE_ORDER</h3> 
      <div class="api-level">
        added in 
       <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/util/Comparator.html">Comparator</a>&lt;<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a>&gt; CASE_INSENSITIVE_ORDER</pre> 
      <p>A Comparator that orders <code>String</code> objects as by <code>compareToIgnoreCase</code>. This comparator is serializable. </p>
      <p> Note that this Comparator does <em>not</em> take locale into account, and will result in an unsatisfactory ordering for certain locales. The java.text package provides <em>Collators</em> to allow locale-sensitive ordering.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <div> 
       <p><b>See also:</b></p> 
       <ul class="nolist">
        <li><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/text/Collator.html#compare(java.lang.String, java.lang.String)">compare(String, String)</a></code></li> 
       </ul> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <!-- Public ctors --> 
     <!-- ========= CONSTRUCTOR DETAIL ======== --> 
     <h2 class="api-section">Public constructors</h2> 
     <a name="String()"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">String</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
String ()</pre> 
      <p>Initializes a newly created <code>String</code> object so that it represents an empty character sequence. Note that use of this constructor is unnecessary since Strings are immutable. </p>
      <p></p> 
     </div> 
     <a name="String(java.lang.String)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">String</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
String (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> original)</pre> 
      <p>Initializes a newly created <code>String</code> object so that it represents the same sequence of characters as the argument; in other words, the newly created string is a copy of the argument string. Unless an explicit copy of <code>original</code> is needed, use of this constructor is unnecessary since Strings are immutable.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>original</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: A <code>String</code> <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="String(char[])"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">String</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
String (char[] value)</pre> 
      <p>Allocates a new <code>String</code> so that it represents the sequence of characters currently contained in the character array argument. The contents of the character array are copied; subsequent modification of the character array does not affect the newly created string.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>value</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>char</code>: The initial value of the string <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="String(char[], int, int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">String</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
String (char[] value, 
                int offset, 
                int count)</pre> 
      <p>Allocates a new <code>String</code> that contains characters from a subarray of the character array argument. The <code>offset</code> argument is the index of the first character of the subarray and the <code>count</code> argument specifies the length of the subarray. The contents of the subarray are copied; subsequent modification of the character array does not affect the newly created string.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>value</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>char</code>: Array that is the source of characters<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>offset</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: The initial offset<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>count</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: The length<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>

         <td width="100%">If the <code>offset</code> and <code>count</code> arguments index characters outside the bounds of the <code>value</code> array </td>

     <a name="String(int[], int, int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">String</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
String (int[] codePoints, 
                int offset, 
                int count)</pre> 
      <p>Allocates a new <code>String</code> that contains characters from a subarray of the <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/Character.html#unicode">Unicode code point</a> array argument. The <code>offset</code> argument is the index of the first code point of the subarray and the <code>count</code> argument specifies the length of the subarray. The contents of the subarray are converted to <code>char</code>s; subsequent modification of the <code>int</code> array does not affect the newly created string.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>codePoints</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: Array that is the source of Unicode code points<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>offset</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: The initial offset<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>count</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: The length<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Throws</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html">IllegalArgumentException</a></code></td> 
         <td width="100%">If any invalid Unicode code point is found in <code>codePoints</code></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/IndexOutOfBoundsException.html">IndexOutOfBoundsException</a></code></td> 
         <td width="100%">If the <code>offset</code> and <code>count</code> arguments index characters outside the bounds of the <code>codePoints</code> array</td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="String(byte[], int, int, int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">String</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
String (byte[] ascii, 
                int hibyte, 
                int offset, 
                int count)</pre> 
      <p> </p>
      <p class="caution"><strong> This constructor was deprecated in API level 1.</strong><br> This method does not properly convert bytes into characters. As of JDK&nbsp;1.1, the preferred way to do this is via the <code>String</code> constructors that take a <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/nio/charset/Charset.html">Charset</a></code>, charset name, or that use the platform's default charset. </p> 
      <p>Allocates a new <code>String</code> constructed from a subarray of an array of 8-bit integer values. </p>
      <p> The <code>offset</code> argument is the index of the first byte of the subarray, and the <code>count</code> argument specifies the length of the subarray. </p>
      <p> Each <code>byte</code> in the subarray is converted to a <code>char</code> as specified in the method above.</p>
      <p></p>

       <tbody>

        </tr>

         <td><code>hibyte</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: The top 8 bits of each 16-bit Unicode code unit<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>offset</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: The initial offset<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>count</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: The length<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Throws</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/IndexOutOfBoundsException.html">IndexOutOfBoundsException</a></code></td> 
         <td width="100%">If the <code>offset</code> or <code>count</code> argument is invalid</td> 
        </tr>

     <a name="String(byte[], int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">String</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
String (byte[] ascii, 
                int hibyte)</pre> 
      <p> </p>
      <p class="caution"><strong> This constructor was deprecated in API level 1.</strong><br> This method does not properly convert bytes into characters. As of JDK&nbsp;1.1, the preferred way to do this is via the <code>String</code> constructors that take a <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/nio/charset/Charset.html">Charset</a></code>, charset name, or that use the platform's default charset. </p> 
      <p>Allocates a new <code>String</code> containing characters constructed from an array of 8-bit integer values. Each character <i>c</i>in the resulting string is constructed from the corresponding component <i>b</i> in the byte array such that: </p>
      <blockquote>
       <pre>
     <b><i>c</i></b> == (char)(((hibyte &amp; 0xff) &lt;&lt; 8)
                         | (<b><i>b</i></b> &amp; 0xff))
 </pre>
      </blockquote>
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>ascii</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>byte</code>: The bytes to be converted to characters<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>hibyte</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: The top 8 bits of each 16-bit Unicode code unit<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table>

     <a name="String(byte[], int, int, java.lang.String)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">String</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
String (byte[] bytes, 
                int offset, 
                int length, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> charsetName)</pre> 
      <p>Constructs a new <code>String</code> by decoding the specified subarray of bytes using the specified charset. The length of the new <code>String</code> is a function of the charset, and hence may not be equal to the length of the subarray. </p>
      <p> The behavior of this constructor when the given bytes are not valid in the given charset is unspecified. The <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/nio/charset/CharsetDecoder.html">CharsetDecoder</a></code> class should be used when more control over the decoding process is required.</p>
      <p></p>

        </tr>

         <td><code>offset</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: The index of the first byte to decode<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>length</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: The number of bytes to decode<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>charsetName</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: The name of a supported <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/nio/charset/Charset.html">charset</a><p></p></td> 
        </tr>

     <a name="String(byte[], int, int, java.nio.charset.Charset)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-9"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">String</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>

        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 9</a>

      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
String (byte[] bytes, 
                int offset, 
                int length, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/nio/charset/Charset.html">Charset</a> charset)</pre> 
      <p>Constructs a new <code>String</code> by decoding the specified subarray of bytes using the specified <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/nio/charset/Charset.html">charset</a>. The length of the new <code>String</code> is a function of the charset, and hence may not be equal to the length of the subarray. </p>
      <p> This method always replaces malformed-input and unmappable-character sequences with this charset's default replacement string. The <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/nio/charset/CharsetDecoder.html">CharsetDecoder</a></code> class should be used when more control over the decoding process is required.</p>

     <a name="String(java.lang.StringBuilder)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">String</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
String (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/StringBuilder.html">StringBuilder</a> builder)</pre> 
      <p>Allocates a new string that contains the sequence of characters currently contained in the string builder argument. The contents of the string builder are copied; subsequent modification of the string builder does not affect the newly created string. </p>
      <p> This constructor is provided to ease migration to <code>StringBuilder</code>. Obtaining a string from a string builder via the <code>toString</code> method is likely to run faster and is generally preferred.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>builder</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>StringBuilder</code>: A <code>StringBuilder</code><p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table>

     <h2 class="api-section">Public methods</h2> 
     <a name="charAt(int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">charAt</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
char charAt (int index)</pre> 
      <p>Returns the <code>char</code> value at the specified index. An index ranges from <code>0</code> to <code>length() - 1</code>. The first <code>char</code> value of the sequence is at index <code>0</code>, the next at index <code>1</code>, and so on, as for array indexing. </p>
      <p>If the <code>char</code> value specified by the index is a <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/Character.html#unicode">surrogate</a>, the surrogate value is returned.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>index</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: the index of the <code>char</code> value.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>char</code></td> 
         <td width="100%">the <code>char</code> value at the specified index of this string. The first <code>char</code> value is at index <code>0</code>.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Throws</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/IndexOutOfBoundsException.html">IndexOutOfBoundsException</a></code></td> 
         <td width="100%">if the <code>index</code> argument is negative or not less than the length of this string. </td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="codePointAt(int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">codePointAt</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
int codePointAt (int index)</pre> 
      <p>Returns the character (Unicode code point) at the specified index. The index refers to <code>char</code> values (Unicode code units) and ranges from <code>0</code> to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html#length()">length()</a></code><code>- 1</code>. </p>
      <p> If the <code>char</code> value specified at the given index is in the high-surrogate range, the following index is less than the length of this <code>String</code>, and the <code>char</code> value at the following index is in the low-surrogate range, then the supplementary code point corresponding to this surrogate pair is returned. Otherwise, the <code>char</code> value at the given index is returned</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr>

         <td><code>index</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: the index to the <code>char</code> values<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>int</code></td> 
         <td width="100%">the code point value of the character at the <code>index</code><p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Throws</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/IndexOutOfBoundsException.html">IndexOutOfBoundsException</a></code></td> 
         <td width="100%">if the <code>index</code> argument is negative or not less than the length of this string.</td> 
        </tr>

     <a name="codePointBefore(int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">codePointBefore</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
int codePointBefore (int index)</pre> 
      <p>Returns the character (Unicode code point) before the specified index. The index refers to <code>char</code> values (Unicode code units) and ranges from <code>1</code> to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/CharSequence.html#length()">length</a></code>. </p>
      <p> If the <code>char</code> value at <code>(index - 1)</code> is in the low-surrogate range, <code>(index - 2)</code> is not negative, and the <code>char</code> value at <code>(index - 2)</code> is in the high-surrogate range, then the supplementary code point value of the surrogate pair is returned. If the <code>char</code> value at <code>index - 1</code> is an unpaired low-surrogate or a high-surrogate, the surrogate value is returned.</p>
      <p></p>

       <tbody>

        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr>

         <td><code>int</code></td> 
         <td width="100%">the Unicode code point value before the given index.<p></p></td> 
        </tr>

      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>

        </tr>

        </tr> 
       </tbody>

     <a name="codePointCount(int, int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">codePointCount</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
int codePointCount (int beginIndex, 
                int endIndex)</pre> 
      <p>Returns the number of Unicode code points in the specified text range of this <code>String</code>. The text range begins at the specified <code>beginIndex</code> and extends to the <code>char</code> at index <code>endIndex - 1</code>. Thus the length (in <code>char</code>s) of the text range is <code>endIndex-beginIndex</code>. Unpaired surrogates within the text range count as one code point each.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>beginIndex</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: the index to the first <code>char</code> of the text range.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>endIndex</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: the index after the last <code>char</code> of the text range.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>int</code></td> 
         <td width="100%">the number of Unicode code points in the specified text range<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Throws</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/IndexOutOfBoundsException.html">IndexOutOfBoundsException</a></code></td> 
         <td width="100%">if the <code>beginIndex</code> is negative, or <code>endIndex</code> is larger than the length of this <code>String</code>, or <code>beginIndex</code> is larger than <code>endIndex</code>.</td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="compareTo(java.lang.String)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">compareTo</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
int compareTo (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> anotherString)</pre> 
      <p>Compares two strings lexicographically. The comparison is based on the Unicode value of each character in the strings. The character sequence represented by this <code>String</code> object is compared lexicographically to the character sequence represented by the argument string. The result is a negative integer if this <code>String</code> object lexicographically precedes the argument string. The result is a positive integer if this <code>String</code> object lexicographically follows the argument string. The result is zero if the strings are equal; <code>compareTo</code> returns <code>0</code> exactly when the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html#equals(java.lang.Object)">equals(Object)</a></code> method would return <code>true</code>. </p>
      <p> This is the definition of lexicographic ordering. If two strings are different, then either they have different characters at some index that is a valid index for both strings, or their lengths are different, or both. If they have different characters at one or more index positions, let <i>k</i> be the smallest such index; then the string whose character at position <i>k</i> has the smaller value, as determined by using the &lt; operator, lexicographically precedes the other string. In this case, <code>compareTo</code> returns the difference of the two character values at position <code>k</code> in the two string -- that is, the value: </p>
      <blockquote>
       <pre>
 this.charAt(k)-anotherString.charAt(k)
 </pre>
      </blockquote> If there is no index position at which they differ, then the shorter string lexicographically precedes the longer string. In this case, 
      <code>compareTo</code> returns the difference of the lengths of the strings -- that is, the value: 
      <blockquote>
       <pre>
 this.length()-anotherString.length()
 </pre>
      </blockquote>
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>anotherString</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: the <code>String</code> to be compared.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>int</code></td> 
         <td width="100%">the value <code>0</code> if the argument string is equal to this string; a value less than <code>0</code> if this string is lexicographically less than the string argument; and a value greater than <code>0</code> if this string is lexicographically greater than the string argument. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="compareToIgnoreCase(java.lang.String)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">compareToIgnoreCase</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
int compareToIgnoreCase (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> str)</pre> 
      <p>Compares two strings lexicographically, ignoring case differences. This method returns an integer whose sign is that of calling <code>compareTo</code> with normalized versions of the strings where case differences have been eliminated by calling <code>Character.toLowerCase(Character.toUpperCase(character))</code> on each character. </p>
      <p> Note that this method does <em>not</em> take locale into account, and will result in an unsatisfactory ordering for certain locales. The java.text package provides <em>collators</em> to allow locale-sensitive ordering.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>str</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: the <code>String</code> to be compared.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>int</code></td> 
         <td width="100%">a negative integer, zero, or a positive integer as the specified String is greater than, equal to, or less than this String, ignoring case considerations.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div> 
       <p><b>See also:</b></p> 
       <ul class="nolist">
        <li><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/text/Collator.html#compare(java.lang.String, java.lang.String)">compare(String, String)</a></code></li> 
       </ul> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <a name="concat(java.lang.String)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">concat</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> concat (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> str)</pre> 
      <p>Concatenates the specified string to the end of this string. </p>
      <p> If the length of the argument string is <code>0</code>, then this <code>String</code> object is returned. Otherwise, a <code>String</code> object is returned that represents a character sequence that is the concatenation of the character sequence represented by this <code>String</code> object and the character sequence represented by the argument string.</p>
      <p> Examples: </p>
      <blockquote>
       <pre>
 "cares".concat("s") returns "caress"
 "to".concat("get").concat("her") returns "together"
 </pre>
      </blockquote>
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr>

         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: the <code>String</code> that is concatenated to the end of this <code>String</code>.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a></code></td> 
         <td width="100%">a string that represents the concatenation of this object's characters followed by the string argument's characters. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div>

     <a name="endsWith(java.lang.String)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">endsWith</h3> 
      <div class="api-level">

        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>

     <a name="equalsIgnoreCase(java.lang.String)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">equalsIgnoreCase</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
boolean equalsIgnoreCase (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> anotherString)</pre> 
      <p>Compares this <code>String</code> to another <code>String</code>, ignoring case considerations. Two strings are considered equal ignoring case if they are of the same length and corresponding characters in the two strings are equal ignoring case. </p>
      <p> Two characters <code>c1</code> and <code>c2</code> are considered the same ignoring case if at least one of the following is true: </p>
      <ul> 
       <li> The two characters are the same (as compared by the <code>==</code> operator) </li>
       <li> Applying the method <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/Character.html#toUpperCase(char)">toUpperCase(char)</a></code> to each character produces the same result </li>
       <li> Applying the method <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/Character.html#toLowerCase(char)">toLowerCase(char)</a></code> to each character produces the same result </li>
      </ul>
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>anotherString</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: The <code>String</code> to compare this <code>String</code> against<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>boolean</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"><code>true</code> if the argument is not <code>null</code> and it represents an equivalent <code>String</code> ignoring case; <code>false</code> otherwise<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table>

     <a name="getBytes(int, int, byte[], int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">getBytes</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void getBytes (int srcBegin, 
                int srcEnd, 
                byte[] dst, 
                int dstBegin)</pre> 
      <p> </p>
      <p class="caution"><strong> This method was deprecated in API level 1.</strong><br> This method does not properly convert characters into bytes. As of JDK&nbsp;1.1, the preferred way to do this is via the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html#getBytes()">getBytes()</a></code> method, which uses the platform's default charset. </p> 
      <p>Copies characters from this string into the destination byte array. Each byte receives the 8 low-order bits of the corresponding character. The eight high-order bits of each character are not copied and do not participate in the transfer in any way. </p>
      <p> The first character to be copied is at index <code>srcBegin</code>; the last character to be copied is at index <code>srcEnd-1</code>. The total number of characters to be copied is <code>srcEnd-srcBegin</code>. The characters, converted to bytes, are copied into the subarray of <code>dst</code> starting at index <code>dstBegin</code> and ending at index: </p>
      <blockquote>
       <pre>
     dstBegin + (srcEnd-srcBegin) - 1
 </pre>
      </blockquote>
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>srcBegin</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: Index of the first character in the string to copy<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>srcEnd</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: Index after the last character in the string to copy<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>dst</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>byte</code>: The destination array<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>dstBegin</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: The start offset in the destination array<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Throws</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/IndexOutOfBoundsException.html">IndexOutOfBoundsException</a></code></td> 
         <td width="100%">If any of the following is true: 
          <ul> 
           <li> <code>srcBegin</code> is negative </li>
           <li> <code>srcBegin</code> is greater than <code>srcEnd</code> </li>
           <li> <code>srcEnd</code> is greater than the length of this String </li>
           <li> <code>dstBegin</code> is negative </li>
           <li> <code>dstBegin+(srcEnd-srcBegin)</code> is larger than <code>dst.length</code> </li>
          </ul> </td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="getChars(int, int, char[], int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">getChars</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void getChars (int srcBegin, 
                int srcEnd, 
                char[] dst, 
                int dstBegin)</pre> 
      <p>Copies characters from this string into the destination character array. </p>
      <p> The first character to be copied is at index <code>srcBegin</code>; the last character to be copied is at index <code>srcEnd-1</code> (thus the total number of characters to be copied is <code>srcEnd-srcBegin</code>). The characters are copied into the subarray of <code>dst</code> starting at index <code>dstBegin</code> and ending at index: </p>
      <blockquote>
       <pre>
     dstBegin + (srcEnd-srcBegin) - 1
 </pre>
      </blockquote>
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>srcBegin</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: index of the first character in the string to copy.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>srcEnd</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: index after the last character in the string to copy.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>dst</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>char</code>: the destination array.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>dstBegin</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: the start offset in the destination array.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Throws</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/IndexOutOfBoundsException.html">IndexOutOfBoundsException</a></code></td> 
         <td width="100%">If any of the following is true: 
          <ul>
           <li><code>srcBegin</code> is negative. </li>
           <li><code>srcBegin</code> is greater than <code>srcEnd</code> </li>
           <li><code>srcEnd</code> is greater than the length of this string </li>
           <li><code>dstBegin</code> is negative </li>
           <li><code>dstBegin+(srcEnd-srcBegin)</code> is larger than <code>dst.length</code></li>
          </ul> </td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="hashCode()"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">hashCode</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
int hashCode ()</pre> 
      <p>Returns a hash code for this string. The hash code for a <code>String</code> object is computed as </p>
      <blockquote>
       <pre>
 s[0]*31^(n-1) + s[1]*31^(n-2) + ... + s[n-1]
 </pre>
      </blockquote> using 
      <code>int</code> arithmetic, where 
      <code>s[i]</code> is the 
      <i>i</i>th character of the string, 
      <code>n</code> is the length of the string, and 
      <code>^</code> indicates exponentiation. (The hash value of the empty string is zero.)
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>int</code></td> 
         <td width="100%">a hash code value for this object. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="indexOf(int, int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">indexOf</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
int indexOf (int ch, 
                int fromIndex)</pre> 
      <p>Returns the index within this string of the first occurrence of the specified character, starting the search at the specified index. </p>
      <p> If a character with value <code>ch</code> occurs in the character sequence represented by this <code>String</code> object at an index no smaller than <code>fromIndex</code>, then the index of the first such occurrence is returned. For values of <code>ch</code> in the range from 0 to 0xFFFF (inclusive), this is the smallest value <i>k</i> such that: </p>
      <blockquote>
       <pre>
 (this.charAt(<i>k</i>) == ch) <code>&amp;&amp;</code> (<i>k</i> &gt;= fromIndex)
 </pre>
      </blockquote> is true. For other values of 
      <code>ch</code>, it is the smallest value 
      <i>k</i> such that: 
      <blockquote>
       <pre>
 (this.codePointAt(<i>k</i>) == ch) <code>&amp;&amp;</code> (<i>k</i> &gt;= fromIndex)
 </pre>
      </blockquote> is true. In either case, if no such character occurs in this string at or after position 
      <code>fromIndex</code>, then 
      <code>-1</code> is returned. 
      <p> There is no restriction on the value of <code>fromIndex</code>. If it is negative, it has the same effect as if it were zero: this entire string may be searched. If it is greater than the length of this string, it has the same effect as if it were equal to the length of this string: <code>-1</code> is returned. </p>
      <p>All indices are specified in <code>char</code> values (Unicode code units).</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>ch</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: a character (Unicode code point).<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>fromIndex</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: the index to start the search from.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>int</code></td> 
         <td width="100%">the index of the first occurrence of the character in the character sequence represented by this object that is greater than or equal to <code>fromIndex</code>, or <code>-1</code> if the character does not occur. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div>

     <a name="intern()"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">intern</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> intern ()</pre> 
      <p>Returns a canonical representation for the string object. </p>
      <p> A pool of strings, initially empty, is maintained privately by the class <code>String</code>. </p>
      <p> When the intern method is invoked, if the pool already contains a string equal to this <code>String</code> object as determined by the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html#equals(java.lang.Object)">equals(Object)</a></code> method, then the string from the pool is returned. Otherwise, this <code>String</code> object is added to the pool and a reference to this <code>String</code> object is returned. </p>
      <p> It follows that for any two strings <code>s</code> and <code>t</code>, <code>s.intern() == t.intern()</code> is <code>true</code> if and only if <code>s.equals(t)</code> is <code>true</code>. </p>
      <p> All literal strings and string-valued constant expressions are interned. String literals are defined in section 3.10.5 of the <cite>The Java Language Specification</cite>.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a></code></td> 
         <td width="100%">a string that has the same contents as this string, but is guaranteed to be from a pool of unique strings. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div>

     <a name="join(java.lang.CharSequence, java.lang.CharSequence...)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-26"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">join</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 26</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> join (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/CharSequence.html">CharSequence</a> delimiter, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/CharSequence.html">CharSequence...</a> elements)</pre> 
      <p>Returns a new String composed of copies of the <code>CharSequence elements</code> joined together with a copy of the specified <code>delimiter</code>. </p>
      <blockquote>
       For example, 
       <pre><code>String message = String.join("-", "Java", "is", "cool");
     // message returned is: "Java-is-cool"
 </code></pre>
      </blockquote> Note that if an element is null, then 
      <code>"null"</code> is added.
      <p></p>
      <p></p>

       <tbody>

        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>elements</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>CharSequence</code>: the elements to join together.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a></code></td> 
         <td width="100%">a new <code>String</code> that is composed of the <code>elements</code> separated by the <code>delimiter</code><p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Throws</th>
        </tr>

         <td width="100%">If <code>delimiter</code> or <code>elements</code> is <code>null</code></td> 
        </tr>

     <a name="lastIndexOf(int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">lastIndexOf</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
int lastIndexOf (int ch)</pre> 
      <p>Returns the index within this string of the last occurrence of the specified character. For values of <code>ch</code> in the range from 0 to 0xFFFF (inclusive), the index (in Unicode code units) returned is the largest value <i>k</i> such that: </p>
      <blockquote>
       <pre>
 this.charAt(<i>k</i>) == ch
 </pre>
      </blockquote> is true. For other values of 
      <code>ch</code>, it is the largest value 
      <i>k</i> such that: 
      <blockquote>
       <pre>
 this.codePointAt(<i>k</i>) == ch
 </pre>
      </blockquote> is true. In either case, if no such character occurs in this string, then 
      <code>-1</code> is returned. The 
      <code>String</code> is searched backwards starting at the last character.
      <p></p>
      <p></p>

     <a name="lastIndexOf(int, int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">lastIndexOf</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
int lastIndexOf (int ch, 
                int fromIndex)</pre> 
      <p>Returns the index within this string of the last occurrence of the specified character, searching backward starting at the specified index. For values of <code>ch</code> in the range from 0 to 0xFFFF (inclusive), the index returned is the largest value <i>k</i> such that: </p>
      <blockquote>
       <pre>
 (this.charAt(<i>k</i>) == ch) <code>&amp;&amp;</code> (<i>k</i> &lt;= fromIndex)
 </pre>
      </blockquote> is true. For other values of 
      <code>ch</code>, it is the largest value 
      <i>k</i> such that: 
      <blockquote>
       <pre>
 (this.codePointAt(<i>k</i>) == ch) <code>&amp;&amp;</code> (<i>k</i> &lt;= fromIndex)
 </pre>
      </blockquote> is true. In either case, if no such character occurs in this string at or before position 
      <code>fromIndex</code>, then 
      <code>-1</code> is returned. 
      <p>All indices are specified in <code>char</code> values (Unicode code units).</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>ch</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: a character (Unicode code point).<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>fromIndex</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: the index to start the search from. There is no restriction on the value of <code>fromIndex</code>. If it is greater than or equal to the length of this string, it has the same effect as if it were equal to one less than the length of this string: this entire string may be searched. If it is negative, it has the same effect as if it were -1: -1 is returned.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>int</code></td> 
         <td width="100%">the index of the last occurrence of the character in the character sequence represented by this object that is less than or equal to <code>fromIndex</code>, or <code>-1</code> if the character does not occur before that point. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div>

     <a name="regionMatches(boolean, int, java.lang.String, int, int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">regionMatches</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
boolean regionMatches (boolean ignoreCase, 
                int toffset, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> other, 
                int ooffset, 
                int len)</pre> 
      <p>Tests if two string regions are equal. </p>
      <p> A substring of this <code>String</code> object is compared to a substring of the argument <code>other</code>. The result is <code>true</code> if these substrings represent character sequences that are the same, ignoring case if and only if <code>ignoreCase</code> is true. The substring of this <code>String</code> object to be compared begins at index <code>toffset</code> and has length <code>len</code>. The substring of <code>other</code> to be compared begins at index <code>ooffset</code> and has length <code>len</code>. The result is <code>false</code> if and only if at least one of the following is true: </p>
      <ul>
       <li><code>toffset</code> is negative. </li>
       <li><code>ooffset</code> is negative. </li>
       <li><code>toffset+len</code> is greater than the length of this <code>String</code> object. </li>
       <li><code>ooffset+len</code> is greater than the length of the other argument. </li>
       <li><code>ignoreCase</code> is <code>false</code> and there is some nonnegative integer <i>k</i> less than <code>len</code> such that: 
        <blockquote>
         <pre>
 this.charAt(toffset+k) != other.charAt(ooffset+k)
 </pre>
        </blockquote> </li>
       <li><code>ignoreCase</code> is <code>true</code> and there is some nonnegative integer <i>k</i> less than <code>len</code> such that: 
        <blockquote>
         <pre>
 Character.toLowerCase(this.charAt(toffset+k)) !=
     Character.toLowerCase(other.charAt(ooffset+k))
 </pre>
        </blockquote> and: 
        <blockquote>
         <pre>
 Character.toUpperCase(this.charAt(toffset+k)) !=
         Character.toUpperCase(other.charAt(ooffset+k))
 </pre>
        </blockquote> </li>
      </ul>
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>ignoreCase</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>boolean</code>: if <code>true</code>, ignore case when comparing characters.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>toffset</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: the starting offset of the subregion in this string.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>other</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: the string argument.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>ooffset</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: the starting offset of the subregion in the string argument.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>len</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: the number of characters to compare.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>boolean</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"><code>true</code> if the specified subregion of this string matches the specified subregion of the string argument; <code>false</code> otherwise. Whether the matching is exact or case insensitive depends on the <code>ignoreCase</code> argument. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="regionMatches(int, java.lang.String, int, int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1">

boolean regionMatches (int toffset, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> other, 
                int ooffset, 
                int len)</pre> 
      <p>Tests if two string regions are equal. </p>
      <p> A substring of this <code>String</code> object is compared to a substring of the argument other. The result is true if these substrings represent identical character sequences. The substring of this <code>String</code> object to be compared begins at index <code>toffset</code> and has length <code>len</code>. The substring of other to be compared begins at index <code>ooffset</code> and has length <code>len</code>. The result is <code>false</code> if and only if at least one of the following is true: </p>
      <ul>
       <li><code>toffset</code> is negative. </li>
       <li><code>ooffset</code> is negative. </li>
       <li><code>toffset+len</code> is greater than the length of this <code>String</code> object. </li>

       <li>There is some nonnegative integer <i>k</i> less than <code>len</code> such that: <code>this.charAt(toffset + </code><i>k</i><code>) != other.charAt(ooffset + </code> <i>k</i><code>)</code> </li>

     <a name="replace(java.lang.CharSequence, java.lang.CharSequence)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">replace</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> replace (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/CharSequence.html">CharSequence</a> target, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/CharSequence.html">CharSequence</a> replacement)</pre> 
      <p>Replaces each substring of this string that matches the literal target sequence with the specified literal replacement sequence. The replacement proceeds from the beginning of the string to the end, for example, replacing "aa" with "b" in the string "aaa" will result in "ba" rather than "ab".</p>
      <p></p>

       <tbody>

        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>replacement</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>CharSequence</code>: The replacement sequence of char values<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a></code></td> 
         <td width="100%">The resulting string<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Throws</th>
